Hive authors `Todo→InProgress` (assign+start), `InReview→Done`/`InReview→InProgress`\n233: (operator review), `*→Cancelled`; the node authors `InProgress→InReview`/`InProgress→Done`, accepted\n234: only with a valid lease + current fencing token. 303 enforces this in `handle_op_batch` (rides P2's\n235: fencing seam — tasks 201/203/205 — as a prose+STOP precondition, not a `depends_on` edge). 304 closes the\n236: SECOND node-status write site (legacy `handle_task_status`).\n237: \n238: | id  | title | dep | conflicts | SC |\n239: |-----|-------|-----|-----------|----|\n240: | 301 | Status transition matrix module — single-author guard table (ADR-0010) | dep: - | conflicts: 302 | SC4 |\n241: | 302 | One canonical status wire value — node→hive mapping boundary helper | dep: 301 | conflicts: 301 303 304 | SC4 |\n242: | 303 | Enforce single-author status transitions at `handle_op_batch` (node gated on lease+token) | dep: 301 302 | conflicts: 302 304 | SC4 |\n243: | 304 | Route the legacy `handle_task_status` write through the transition guard | dep: 301 303 | conflicts: 302 303 | SC4 |\n244: \n245: ## Execution preconditions & closeout (READ — affects whether the gate passes)\n246: \n247: - **Rust gate overrides:** every Rust task sets `WAI_TYPECHECK_CMD=\"cargo check -p <crate>\"` (or\n248:   `--workspace`) and `WAI_TEST_CMD=\"cargo test -p <crate> <test>\"` in its `## Done when` (Trap 1).\n249: - **SQLx offline:** tasks adding/changing a `query!`/`query_as!` export\n250:   `DATABASE_URL=sqlite://<repo>/dev_assets/db.sqlite` against a migrated dev DB; **no task runs\n251:   `cargo sqlx prepare`** (Trap 2). The hive (Postgres) side has its own offline considerations — see\n252:   the trap ledger's remote-crate analogue.\n253: - **Closeout (NOT a gated task):** after all schema/query tasks land, regenerate the `.sqlx` cache once\n254:   and commit it as a standalone housekeeping commit at `/wai:close`.\n255: \n256: ## SC coverage map (enforced ids SC1–SC7)\n257: \n258: SC1→{phase-6 no-fanout (data-plane half); UI half carve-gated} · SC2→{phase-1} · SC3→{phase-2} ·\n259: SC4→{phase-3} · SC5→{phase-5} · SC6→{phase-7} · SC7→{phase-4}. (Clause sub-ids SC2a/b/c, SC3 fencing,\n260: SC5d-style negatives are mapped to specific tasks at authoring time.)\n\n(End of file - total 260 lines)\n</content>","metadata":{"preview":"---\ntopic: vk-swarm-hive-redesign\ndoc_type: plan\nstatus: draft\nspec: docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-26-vk-swarm-hive-redesign.md\n---\n\n# Plan — vk-swarm-hive-redesign\n\n## Approach\n\nRebuild the node↔hive reconciliation contract as a hub-and-spoke control plane, keeping the storage\nengines (Postgres hive store, SQLite node-of-record, WS transport). The work spans **both ends of a\nnetwork protocol** and is sequenced so the **foundation flows end-to-end before anything rides it**:\nthe ordered, acknowledged op-log (SC2) is the channel every later guarantee depends on, so it ships\nfirst as a tracer bullet — one op type flowing node→hive with a durable ack — then the remaining op\ntypes, then the mechanisms that ride it (fencing, status machine, anti-entropy). The inbound-channel\ncollapse (SC7) and the cutover migration (SC6) are comparatively independent and ship in their own\nphases.\n","truncated":false,"loaded":[],"display":{"type":"file","path":"/home/david/Code/vk-swarm/.claude/worktrees/bridge-cse_01B8B52jjMEdikaLRoA25qhr/docs/plans/vk-swarm-hive-redesign/plan.md","text":"---\ntopic: vk-swarm-hive-redesign\ndoc_type: plan\nstatus: draft\nspec: docs/superpowers/specs/2026-06-26-vk-swarm-hive-redesign.md\n---\n\n# Plan — vk-swarm-hive-redesign\n\n## Approach\n\nRebuild the node↔hive reconciliation contract as a hub-and-spoke control plane, keeping the storage\nengines (Postgres hive store, SQLite node-of-record, WS transport). The work spans **both ends of a\nnetwork protocol** and is sequenced so the **foundation flows end-to-end before anything rides it**:\nthe ordered, acknowledged op-log (SC2) is the channel every later guarantee depends on, so it ships\nfirst as a tracer bullet — one op type flowing node→hive with a durable ack — then the remaining op\ntypes, then the mechanisms that ride it (fencing, status machine, anti-entropy). The inbound-channel\ncollapse (SC7) and the cutover migration (SC6) are comparatively independent and ship in their own\nphases.\n\nEvery task is Rust (or a migration/CI/frontend task). **This repo is a Cargo workspace, so the WAI\ngate's TypeScript type-check is skipped and its `scope_test` runner has no native `cargo test` path** —\nevery Rust task carries explicit `WAI_TYPECHECK_CMD`/`WAI_TEST_CMD` overrides (decisions-ledger Trap 1).\n**SQLx is offline-mode** (committed `.sqlx` cache, `DATABASE_URL` unset): schema/query tasks execute\nagainst a live migrated dev DB and never run `cargo sqlx prepare` in a gated task (Trap 2). Adding any\n`NodeMessage`/`ServerMessage` WS variant (the op-log/ack/heartbeat/lease messages) hits the\n**enum-exhaustiveness trap on BOTH ends** (Trap 3) — every match arm in the same commit. Anchors were\nauthored against current `main`; the adversarial breakdown tournament re-verifies each before any code.\n\n**This decompose covers the protocol + data plane (SC2–SC7 and the no-fan-out, data-plane half of\nSC1).** The *hive central-management web UI* half of SC1 is a carve candidate (see Scope note) decided\nwith the user before task authoring, mirroring the node-foundations → `vk-swarm-node-ui-localize` split.\n\nPhase dependency spine: **P1 (op-log) → P2 (fencing) → P3 (status machine)**; **P1 → P5 (anti-entropy)**;\n**P4 (inbound collapse)** is independent of the spine; **P7 (cutover migration)** depends on the\nrebuilt schema (P1–P3); **P6 (no fan-out)** is data-plane and independent.\n\n## Phases\n\n1. **phase-1-oplog** — node→hive single ordered, acknowledged op-log/outbox: outbox table, op append on\n   local writes, WS stream in seq order, hive idempotent apply + durable ack, cursor-advance-on-ack,\n   parent-before-child parking. Replaces the five push paths (SC2). *Foundation.*\n2. **phase-2-lease-fencing** — assignment via atomic checkout + lease (`lease_expires_at`), heartbeat\n   renewal, monotonic fencing token on grants and on op-log ops, hive stale-token rejection, node\n   self-fencing (reuses the ADR-0001 process fence). Discharges node-foundations D7 (SC3). Depends P1.\n3. **phase-3-status-machine** — explicit `task.status` transition matrix, single-author enforcement\n   (hive vs node, gated on lease+token), status enum value canonicalization (SC4). Depends P1, P2.\n4. **phase-4-inbound-collapse** — WS activity stream as the single live inbound channel; bulk snapshot\n   demoted to reconcile-only; remove the dead Electric task-shape path; one delete semantic\n   (soft-unlink + tombstone); node dirty-guard conflict policy; handle `task.reassigned` (SC7).\n5. **phase-5-anti-entropy** — digest exchange (per-entity version/hash + outbox high-water) over the\n   op-log, gap heal replacing manual `reset_*` migrations (SC5). Depends P1 (+P4 reconcile leg).\n6. **phase-6-no-fanout** — **verify + guard** that nodes receive only assignment/ack traffic, never\n   pushed shared-task state (SC1 data-plane half). Investigation found this is *already* true today —\n   the node-facing channel carries only `ProjectSync`/`NodeRemoved` — so phase-6 asserts and fences the\n   invariant against regression; it is NOT a large fan-out removal. Browser-facing shared-task fan-out\n   (electric_proxy/ActivityBroker) is the hive-UI data source and is OUT of scope. Depends P1, P2.\n7. **phase-7-cutover** — one-time hive-only-state migration (migrate / regenerate / discard per\n   ADR-0011), preserving the node↔hive id bridge and remapping status enum values (SC6). Depends P1–P3.\n\n## Scope note — SC1 central-management UI CARVED to `vk-swarm-hive-ui`\n\nSC1 has two halves: (a) the **data-plane** guarantee \"no node↔node / node↔hive↔node fan-out\" (covered\nhere, phase-6), and (b) the **hive web UI manages all** nodes/projects/tasks/attempts/executions.\n**User decision (2026-06-30): half (b) is carved into `vk-swarm-hive-ui`** (tracker seeded; rehost +\nrewire + net-new cross-node views — see that README and the decisions ledger). This plan covers SC2–SC7\n+ SC1's data-plane half. SC1 stays in the frozen spec, claimed by phase-6; no spec edit was made.\n\n## Task table\n\n`dep:`/`conflicts:` mirror each task's frontmatter (wai-plan-lint enforces equality). `-` = none.\n**Phase 1 is authored (this pass); Phases 2–7 are authored in subsequent `/wai:decompose` passes** as\neach prior ships (user-approved phase-by-phase, decisions-ledger).\n\n### Phase 1 — op-log foundation (SC2; authored as a safe additive tracer, op_type `task.upsert`)\n\n| id  | title | dep | conflicts | SC |\n|-----|-------|-----|-----------|----|\n| 101 | Add `node_outbox` table migration (SQLite) | dep: - | conflicts: none | SC2a |\n| 102 | Add `node_op_log` table migration (Postgres/hive) | dep: - | conflicts: none | SC2c |\n| 103 | Add `OpBatch`/`OutboxOp`/`OpAck` WS variants to both crates + exhaustive stub arms | dep: - | conflicts: 106 108 | SC2a |\n| 104 | Add node `OutboxRepository` (enqueue/peek_unacked/mark_acked_through) | dep: 101 | conflicts: none | SC2a |\n| 105 | Enqueue a `task.upsert` op on `Task::create`/`update` | dep: 104 | conflicts: none | SC2b |\n| 106 | Hive `handle_op_batch` — idempotent apply + park/skip + durable `OpAck` | dep: 102 103 | conflicts: 103 | SC2c |\n| 107 | Node streamer — drain `node_outbox` into `OpBatch` in `sync_once` | dep: 103 104 | conflicts: none | SC2a |\n| 108 | Node `OpAck` — advance ack cursor on durable hive ack | dep: 103 104 | conflicts: 103 | SC2c |\n\n> **Tracer honesty (recorded in the ledger):** Phase 1 proves the ordered-ack'd round-trip *mechanism*\n> alongside the legacy paths. It does NOT yet fully discharge SC2 — (i) `105`'s enqueue is non-atomic\n> with the task write, so true SC2c no-loss needs a transactional enqueue; (ii) only `task.upsert`\n> flows; (iii) the five legacy push paths are NOT retired. Those are the next Phase-1 increment.\n\n### Phase 2 — lease / atomic-checkout + fencing (SC3; ADR-0009; discharges node-foundations D7)\n\nAtomic conditional checkout (`try_claim`) + real lease (`lease_expires_at`) + monotonic `fencing_token`\n(per-hive `node_fencing_token_seq`). The node renews via `LeaseHeartbeat`; the hive replies `LeaseGrant`\n(token+expiry). The node stamps `OutboxOp.fencing_token` for hive-assigned tasks **at op-stream time** from\nits lease state (the `db`-crate enqueue cannot know leases — ledger), and the hive **rejects** any op whose\ntoken is older than the assignment's current token (the at-most-once commit effect). A node that loses its\nlease **self-fences** (reuses the ADR-0001 `stop_execution` kill via `AssignmentHandler::handle_cancellation`).\nA background sweep (`stale_cleanup.rs` analog) reclaims expired leases with a bumped token. Variant shapes\nare FIXED by CONTRACT §A; schema by §B; fencing semantics by §C.\n\n| id  | title | dep | conflicts | SC |\n|-----|-------|-----|-----------|----|\n| 201 | Add `lease_expires_at`+`fencing_token` cols + `node_fencing_token_seq` (Postgres) | dep: - | conflicts: none | SC3 |\n| 202 | Add `LeaseHeartbeat`/`LeaseGrant`/`LeaseRevoked` WS variants to both crates + stub arms | dep: - | conflicts: 204 205 206 | SC3 |\n| 203 | Hive `TaskAssignmentRepository::try_claim` (atomic CAS) + `renew_lease` | dep: 201 | conflicts: 209 | SC3 |\n| 204 | Hive `handle_lease_heartbeat` — renew leases, reply `LeaseGrant` per assignment | dep: 202 203 | conflicts: 202 205 | SC3 |\n| 205 | Hive fencing enforcement in `handle_op_batch` — reject stale-token, emit `LeaseRevoked` | dep: 106 202 203 | conflicts: 202 204 | SC3 |\n| 206 | Node lease state — `HiveEvent` lease variants, token+expiry on `ActiveAssignment`, send `LeaseHeartbeat` | dep: 202 | conflicts: 202 207 208 | SC3 |\n| 207 | Node — stamp `OutboxOp.fencing_token` from the lease at stream time (hive-assigned tasks only) | dep: 107 206 | conflicts: 206 208 | SC3 |\n| 208 | Node self-fence watchdog — halt the agent on lease-revoke / renew-deadline miss | dep: 206 | conflicts: 206 207 | SC3 |\n| 209 | Hive lease-expiry sweep — reclaim expired leases with a bumped token (timer, analog stale_cleanup) | dep: 201 203 | conflicts: 203 | SC3 |\n| 210 | SC3 acceptance test — partition cannot double-execute (stale-token reject + self-fence) | dep: 203 205 208 209 | conflicts: none | SC3 |\n\n> **Phase-2 honesty:** SC3's guarantee is \"at-most-once commit *effect* (stale-token rejection, 205) +\n> bounded-overlap execution (node self-fence, 208)\" — NOT \"we have leases\" (ADR-0009). 210 claims TS2 and\n> proves the hive reject leg end-to-end; the node self-fence leg is proven by 206/208's hermetic unit tests\n> (a true cross-process WS round-trip is out of hermetic scope — recorded in the ledger). The lease state\n> lives on `ActiveAssignment` (one structure serves 206/207/208) — a reconciled design decision (ledger).\n> **Cross-phase shared files:** 205 EDITS `handle_op_batch` (authored by P1/106) — `depends_on: 106`. The\n> WS enum files (`message.rs`, `hive_client.rs`), `session.rs`, and `node_runner.rs` are touched in BOTH\n> P1 and P2 (and later phases); the orchestrator reconciles cross-phase conflicts on them.\n\n### Phase 5 — anti-entropy reconciliation digest (SC5; rides P1's op-log, TS4 self-heal)\n\nRiding the P1 op-log (ADR-0008): the node periodically (and on the first sync cycle after reconnect)\nemits a per-entity **version digest** of its swarm-linked tasks; the hive compares it against\n`shared_tasks`/`node_op_log` and replies a **DigestResult** that directs the heal —\n`resend_from_seq` re-streams the node's op-log (node-has/hive-lacks, including acked-but-lost ops via the\nnew `peek_from_seq`) and `pull_entities` triggers the bulk-snapshot reconcile leg (hive-has/node-lacks).\nThis **replaces the manual `reset_*` repair migrations**; convergence is the protocol path only, no\nout-of-band SQL. The `Digest`/`DigestResult` variant shapes are FIXED by CONTRACT §A.\n\n| id  | title | dep | conflicts | SC |\n|-----|-------|-----|-----------|----|\n| 501 | Add `Digest`/`DigestEntry`/`DigestResult` WS variants to both crates + exhaustive stub arms | dep: - | conflicts: 503 504 | SC5 |\n| 502 | Node digest builder — emit `NodeMessage::Digest` of swarm-linked tasks each sync cycle | dep: 501 | conflicts: none | SC5 |\n| 503 | Hive `handle_digest` — compare vs `shared_tasks`/`node_op_log`, reply `DigestResult` (TS4 self-heal) | dep: 501 | conflicts: 501 | SC5 |\n| 504 | Node acts on `DigestResult` — re-stream from `resend_from_seq` + pull via reconcile leg | dep: 501 502 | conflicts: 501 | SC5 |\n\n> **Cross-phase shared-file collision (CONTRACT §A, recorded in the ledger).** 501 hand-duplicates the\n> `Digest`/`DigestResult` variants into `crates/services/src/services/hive_client.rs` AND\n> `crates/remote/src/nodes/ws/message.rs` (+ exhaustive arms in `session.rs`) — the SAME two enum files\n> P2's lease-protocol task edits (`LeaseHeartbeat`/`LeaseGrant`/`LeaseRevoked`). The two protocol tasks\n> `conflicts_with` each other; P2 is **not yet authored as ids**, so 501's frontmatter carries only the\n> intra-P5 conflicts. When P2 lands, its protocol task MUST add 501 to its `conflicts_with` (and 501 is\n> updated symmetrically) and be `depends_on`-sequenced so the two never edit the enum tails at once.\n> 503 also edits `crates/remote/src/nodes/ws/session.rs` and `crates/remote/src/db/tasks.rs`; 504 also\n> edits `crates/db/src/models/node_outbox.rs` and `crates/services/src/services/node_runner.rs`.\n\n### Phase 6 — no fan-out (SC1 data-plane half; VERIFY + GUARD, not a removal)\n\nVerified in code (decisions-ledger): the node-facing channel already carries only\n`ProjectSync`/`NodeRemoved` (+ per-node control/own-assignment/own-backfill), NOT shared-task state.\nPhase-6 asserts and fences that invariant against regression; it is NOT a large fan-out removal.\n\n| id  | title | dep | conflicts | SC |\n|-----|-------|-----|-----------|----|\n| 601 | No-fanout invariant guard — exhaustive `HiveMessage` classification + topology assertion (hermetic, no DB) | dep: 103 | conflicts: none | SC1 |\n| 602 | No-fanout send-site comment fence — document the SC1 invariant at `connection.rs` | dep: 601 | conflicts: none | SC1 |\n\n> **601 `depends_on: 103` (the enum-drift fence).** Phase-6 is sequenced after P1/P2/P5, which ADD\n> hive→node `HiveMessage` variants (`OpAck`@P1-task-103, `LeaseGrant`/`LeaseRevoked`@P2,\n> `DigestResult`@P5 — CONTRACT §A). 601's classification `match` is exhaustive over `HiveMessage`, so it\n> must see the GROWN enum, not main's. The dep on the authored variant-adding task **103** makes the\n> ordering explicit; the P2/P5 variants (whose tasks are not yet authored as ids) are **decision-locked**\n> in 601's body (a fixed `variant → Delivery` table the executor applies — none is fan-out), so the guard\n> never devolves to executor judgment when those variants land.\n\n### Phase 7 — hive-only-state cutover (SC6 / TS6; ADR-0011 migrate / regenerate / discard)\n\n**In-place rebuild — judgment call ratified at authoring (NEEDS ORCHESTRATOR/USER RATIFICATION).** No\ntask in this workstream rebuilds the hive schema; every REGENERABLE/DISCARDABLE table still has surviving\n`query!` refs in `crates/remote/src` (code removal is P4/P5, out of scope here), and the node re-ingest\npath `INSERT`s into the existing table (`node_task_attempts.rs:52`). So the cutover is a **DATA operation\n(TRUNCATE/DELETE), NOT a schema DROP**: MUST-MIGRATE tables (incl. the `source_task_id`/`source_node_id`\nid bridge) stay in place, and the hive `task_status` enum is already canonical kebab-case (the\n`inprogress`→`in-progress` remap is at the node→hive ingest boundary, not at rest). The destructive\nalternative (copy MUST-MIGRATE into a fresh empty schema) is NOT authored; each task STOPs if it is\nmandated instead.\n\n| id  | title | dep | conflicts | SC |\n|-----|-------|-----|-----------|----|\n| 701 | Cutover migration — data-clear REGENERABLE + DISCARDABLE hive-only state (in-place) | dep: - | conflicts: none | SC6 |\n| 702 | Cutover guard — MUST-MIGRATE round-trip: id bridge intact + status canonical | dep: 701 | conflicts: none | SC6 |\n| 703 | Cutover guard — REGENERABLE tables repopulate from a simulated node re-ingest | dep: 701 | conflicts: none | SC6 |\n\n> **701 is `irreversible: true`** (data loss; gated behind a pre-cutover backup, ADR-0011) — needs a\n> `reviews/701.approved` token before its gate runs. All three are Postgres + fail-closed (Trap 2b): the\n> `## Done when` carries `test -n \"$DATABASE_URL\" && cargo test …` so a no-DB run fails instead of a\n> hollow skipped green. 701's test is **seed → run the cutover SQL → assert** (not connect-and-count) so\n> it is non-hollow even though the migration ran at `migrate!` time on an empty DB. 703 carries a\n> ratified FIDELITY limitation: it drives the EXISTING `NodeTaskAttemptRepository::upsert` re-ingest path\n> (the new ADR-0008 op-log re-ingest for attempts does not exist yet — P1 shipped only `task.upsert`),\n> proving the schema is refillable post-cutover, not the op-log mechanism.\n>\n> **FROZEN-SPEC COLLISION (NEEDS RATIFICATION):** spec TS6 says \"discardable tables are **absent**\"; the\n> in-place reading keeps them present-but-emptied (their code refs are removed only in P4/P5, and P7\n> depends on P1–P3). Ratify keep-but-empty (option a, authored) OR sequence a follow-up DROP after the\n> P4/P5 code-removal (option b). See the decisions-ledger Phase-7 item 2b.\n\n### Phase 4 — inbound collapse (SC7 / TS5; authored this pass — ADR-0007)\n\n| id  | title | dep | conflicts | SC |\n|-----|-------|-----|-----------|----|\n| 401 | TS5 acceptance — single inbound channel, one delete, one conflict + topology guard | dep: 402 403 404 | conflicts: 402 403 | SC7 |\n| 402 | One delete semantic — both inbound legs soft-unlink via a single shared helper | dep: - | conflicts: 401 403 404 | SC7 |\n| 403 | Dirty-guard in `upsert_remote_task` — inbound never clobbers an unacked local edit | dep: 104 | conflicts: 401 402 | SC7 |\n| 404 | Handle `task.reassigned` in the activity processor — no dropped event types | dep: - | conflicts: 402 | SC7 |\n| 405 | Remove the dead `ElectricTaskSyncService` task-shape path (IRREVERSIBLE) | dep: - | conflicts: none | SC7 |\n\n> **Phase-4 authoring notes (recorded in the ledger):** (i) the bulk-snapshot reconcile is ALREADY\n> connect-gated (its only caller is the `HiveEvent::Connected` arm; no periodic task re-sync exists), so\n> \"demote to cold-start/gap-fill\" is a **verify + guard** (401's comment fence + topology STOP-trigger),\n> NOT a removal — mirrors the SC1 no-fanout \"already satisfied\" finding. This is a known divergence from rubric #3's \"exact Before/After\"; the\n   tournament will probe it — defensible because the behavior is test-pinned and the SQL is schema-dependent.\n   (203's `LeaseClaim.lease_expires_at` is coordinated to `Option` so 209's reclaim, which NULLs it, fits the","truncated":false,"loaded":[],"display":{"type":"file","path":"/home/david/Code/vk-swarm/.claude/worktrees/bridge-cse_01B8B52jjMEdikaLRoA25qhr/docs/plans/vk-swarm-hive-redesign/decisions-ledger.md","text":"   param would break P1/107's test + every existing `HiveSyncService::new` caller. **Decision:** add an\n   `Option<Arc<RwLock<NodeRunnerState>>>` field + a `with_node_state` builder; `None` = passthrough (the 107\n   behavior); only the live node spawn passes `Some`. Resolved by fencing on EXPIRY (`Some(exp) < now`) only and letting the\n   explicit revoke event fence directly — recorded in 208's STOP triggers for the executor to pin.\n\n6. **203/205/209 specify the hard SQL as a CONTRACT (`todo!` + tests), not literal Before/After.** The\n   atomic CAS (`try_claim`), the fencing reject control-flow, and the reclaim UPDATE interact with the live\n   `idx_task_assignments_active` partial unique index and the available-vs-expired split, which must be\n   finalized against the live schema. **Decision (deliberate, not an omission):** the method signatures +\n   the per-method test set (4 for 203, 3 for 205, 2 for 209) pin the OBSERVABLE contract; the executor writes\n   the statement that satisfies them. This is a known divergence from rubric #3's \"exact Before/After\"; the\n   tournament will probe it — defensible because the behavior is test-pinned and the SQL is schema-dependent.\n   (203's `LeaseClaim.lease_expires_at` is coordinated to `Option` so 209's reclaim, which NULLs it, fits the\n   same struct.)\n\n7. **TS2 proven as two coordinated legs, not a cross-process round-trip (210).** A real node binary ↔ real\n   hive WS round-trip is not hermetically testable in one `cargo test`. **Decision:** 210 proves the hive\n   stale-token REJECT leg (the at-most-once commit effect) against live PG; the node SELF-FENCE leg (bounded\n   overlap) is proven by 206/208's hermetic unit tests, asserted by reference in 210 + recorded here. 210\n   claims TS2 (the only task that does — required or `wai-plan-lint` hard-fails on unclaimed TS2).\n\n**Trap-1/Trap-2b adherence:** every hive task (201,203,204,205,209,210) sets `WAI_TYPECHECK_CMD=\"cargo check\n-p remote\"` + a FAIL-CLOSED `WAI_TEST_CMD='test -n \"$DATABASE_URL\" && cargo test -p remote …'`, and its\nPG-touching test is a `#[cfg(test)] mod` (private handlers) or a `tests/` integration test with inlined\n`skip_without_db!`. The paperclip\n12: reference gives the proven *shape* — an atomic conditional checkout\n13: (`UPDATE issues SET checkoutRunId=… WHERE status IN (…) RETURNING`, `paperclip/services/issues.ts:5533-5728`)\n14: and an escalate-don't-kill silence watchdog — but paperclip runs each agent as a **server-owned local\n15: subprocess**, so it has **no remote-worker network hop**: its \"lease\" is derived from a locally-observed\n16: process, not a timed lease, and it has no defence against a *partitioned-but-still-alive* worker.\n17: \n18: vk-swarm's hive↔node boundary **is** that network hop. **Leases + heartbeats alone are not enough:** if\n19: the hive leases task T to node A, A partitions but keeps running, the lease expires, and the hive\n20: reclaims T to node B — then A and B both execute T. Liveness detection, reclaim, and idempotent claim do\n21: not stop the partitioned-but-alive writer.\n22: \n23: node-foundations [ADR-0001](./0001-crash-recovery-fence-then-resume.md) already established a\n24: process-group fence (PID + start-time fingerprint, defeating PID reuse) and explicitly punted\n25: cross-node ownership (D7) to this workstream.\n26: \n27: ## Decision\n28: \n29: 1. **Atomic checkout (idempotent claim).** The hive assigns via a conditional CAS —\n30:    `UPDATE node_task_assignments SET node_id=?, lease_expires_at=?, fencing_token=<next> WHERE <task\n31:    available> RETURNING` — so two nodes can never both win a claim (port of paperclip's\n32:    `UPDATE … RETURNING`).\n33: 2. **Real lease with expiry + heartbeat renewal.** Each grant has a `lease_expires_at`; the node\n34:    renews via a periodic heartbeat carrying its node id and in-flight assignment ids. A missed\n35:    heartbeat lets the lease expire; the hive may then reclaim/reassign with a **new, strictly higher\n36:    fencing token**.\n37: 3. **Fencing tokens (the partition-safety mechanism), scoped to hive-assigned tasks.** Every lease\n38:    grant carries a monotonic fencing token. The node stamps every report-up op\n39:    ([ADR-0008](./0008-node-hive-ordered-ack-outbox.md)) **against a hive-assigned task** with that\n40:    task's current token; the hive **rejects any commit whose token is older than the assignment's\n41:    current token**. So a partitioned node A, after its lease is reassigned to B (higher token), has its\n42:    late writes **bounced** → **at-most-once commit effect**. **Node-owned work** (locally-created tasks\n43:    and their attempts/execs/logs) has no assignment and no lease — those ops carry **no fencing token**\n44:    and are committed under the node's **ownership identity** (the node is the sole authority for its own\n45:    tasks), so the stale-token check simply does not apply to them.\n46: 4. **Node self-fencing (bounds the overlap).** A node that cannot renew within the lease TTL **halts\n47:    the agent** — the process-group kill from [ADR-0001](./0001-crash-recovery-fence-then-resume.md) —\n48:    so execution overlap is **bounded**, not unbounded.\n49: \n50: **Guarantee stated precisely:** at-most-once commit *effect* (fencing token rejection) + bounded-overlap\n51: execution (node self-fencing). This is what \"a partition cannot cause double execution\" means in a\n52: network system — not \"we have leases\".\n53: \n54: ## Consequences\n55: \n56: - Satisfies SC3 and **discharges node-foundations D7**: foreign-row disambiguation on the hive is now\n57:   lease/ownership-based, not the single-node `!= current_instance` heuristic.\n58: - Adds a heartbeat/renewal path and a `fencing_token` column on assignments and on every op\n59:   (wire-format change, irreversible).\n60: - Self-fencing reuses an existing mechanism (ADR-0001), so the only new node behaviour is the\n61:   renew-deadline watchdog.\n62: \n63: ## Alternatives considered\n64: \n65: - **Lease + heartbeat without fencing** — rejected: does not stop the partitioned-but-alive writer\n66:   (the exact SC3 failure).\n67: - **Paperclip's terminal-status-derived lock** (no timed lease) — rejected: depends on the server\n68:   directly observing the agent process, which the hive cannot do across the network.\n69: - **Distributed lock service (etcd/Consul)** — rejected: heavy new dependency; a Postgres CAS + fencing\n70:   token meets the guarantee within the existing store.\n\n(End of file - total 70 lines)\n</content>","metadata":{"preview":"# ADR-0009 — Assignment via atomic checkout + lease, made partition-safe by fencing tokens\n\n- **Status:** accepted\n- **Date:** 2026-06-30\n- **Workstream:** vk-swarm-hive-redesign\n- **Discharges:** node-foundations **D7** / [ADR-0001](./0001-crash-recovery-fence-then-resume.md)\n  (`mark_orphaned_as_failed` matching foreign nodes' rows — punted to this workstream)\n\n## Context\n\nSC3 requires that a **network partition cannot cause double execution** of the same task. The paperclip\nreference gives the proven *shape* — an atomic conditional checkout\n(`UPDATE issues SET checkoutRunId=… WHERE status IN (…) RETURNING`, `paperclip/services/issues.ts:5533-5728`)\nand an escalate-don't-kill silence watchdog — but paperclip runs each agent as a **server-owned local\nsubprocess**, so it has **no remote-worker network hop**: its \"lease\" is derived from a locally-observed\nprocess, not a timed lease, and it has no defence against a *partitioned-but-still-alive* worker.\n\nvk-swarm's hive↔node boundary **is** that network hop. **Leases + heartbeats alone are not enough:** if\nthe hive leases task T to node A, A partitions but keeps running, the lease expires, and the hive\nreclaims T to node B — then A and B both execute T. Liveness detection, reclaim, and idempotent claim do","truncated":false,"loaded":[],"display":{"type":"file","path":"/home/david/Code/vk-swarm/.claude/worktrees/bridge-cse_01B8B52jjMEdikaLRoA25qhr/dev-docs/adr/0009-lease-checkout-fencing.md","text":"# ADR-0009 — Assignment via atomic checkout + lease, made partition-safe by fencing tokens\n\n- **Status:** accepted\n- **Date:** 2026-06-30\n- **Workstream:** vk-swarm-hive-redesign\n- **Discharges:** node-foundations **D7** / [ADR-0001](./0001-crash-recovery-fence-then-resume.md)\n  (`mark_orphaned_as_failed` matching foreign nodes' rows — punted to this workstream)\n\n## Context\n\nSC3 requires that a **network partition cannot cause double execution** of the same task. The paperclip\nreference gives the proven *shape* — an atomic conditional checkout\n(`UPDATE issues SET checkoutRunId=… WHERE status IN (…) RETURNING`, `paperclip/services/issues.ts:5533-5728`)\nand an escalate-don't-kill silence watchdog — but paperclip runs each agent as a **server-owned local\nsubprocess**, so it has **no remote-worker network hop**: its \"lease\" is derived from a locally-observed\nprocess, not a timed lease, and it has no defence against a *partitioned-but-still-alive* worker.\n\nvk-swarm's hive↔node boundary **is** that network hop. **Leases + heartbeats alone are not enough:** if\nthe hive leases task T to node A, A partitions but keeps running, the lease expires, and the hive\nreclaims T to node B — then A and B both execute T. Liveness detection, reclaim, and idempotent claim do\nnot stop the partitioned-but-alive writer.\n\nnode-foundations [ADR-0001](./0001-crash-recovery-fence-then-resume.md) already established a\nprocess-group fence (PID + start-time fingerprint, defeating PID reuse) and explicitly punted\ncross-node ownership (D7) to this workstream.\n\n## Decision\n\n1. **Atomic checkout (idempotent claim).** The hive assigns via a conditional CAS —\n   `UPDATE node_task_assignments SET node_id=?, lease_expires_at=?, fencing_token=<next> WHERE <task\n   available> RETURNING` — so two nodes can never both win a claim (port of paperclip's\n   `UPDATE … RETURNING`).\n2. **Real lease with expiry + heartbeat renewal.** Each grant has a `lease_expires_at`; the node\n   renews via a periodic heartbeat carrying its node id and in-flight assignment ids. A missed\n   heartbeat lets the lease expire; the hive may then reclaim/reassign with a **new, strictly higher\n   fencing token**.\n3. **Fencing tokens (the partition-safety mechanism), scoped to hive-assigned tasks.** Every lease\n   grant carries a monotonic fencing token. The node stamps every report-up op\n   ([ADR-0008](./0008-node-hive-ordered-ack-outbox.md)) **against a hive-assigned task** with that\n   task's current token; the hive **rejects any commit whose token is older than the assignment's\n   current token**. So a partitioned node A, after its lease is reassigned to B (higher token), has its\n   late writes **bounced** → **at-most-once commit effect**. **Node-owned work** (locally-created tasks\n   and their attempts/execs/logs) has no assignment and no lease — those ops carry **no fencing token**\n   and are committed under the node's **ownership identity** (the node is the sole authority for its own\n   tasks), so the stale-token check simply does not apply to them.\n4. **Node self-fencing (bounds the overlap).** A node that cannot renew within the lease TTL **halts\n   the agent** — the process-group kill from [ADR-0001](./0001-crash-recovery-fence-then-resume.md) —\n   so execution overlap is **bounded**, not unbounded.\n\n**Guarantee stated precisely:** at-most-once commit *effect* (fencing token rejection) + bounded-overlap\nexecution (node self-fencing). This is what \"a partition cannot cause double execution\" means in a\nnetwork system — not \"we have leases\".\n\n## Consequences\n\n- Satisfies SC3 and **discharges node-foundations D7**: foreign-row disambiguation on the hive is now\n  lease/ownership-based, not the single-node `!= current_instance` heuristic.\n- Adds a heartbeat/renewal path and a `fencing_token` column on assignments and on every op\n  (wire-format change, irreversible).\n- Self-fencing reuses an existing mechanism (ADR-0001), so the only new node behaviour is the\n  renew-deadline watchdog.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- **Lease + heartbeat without fencing** — rejected: does not stop the partitioned-but-alive writer\n  (the exact SC3 failure).\n- **Paperclip's terminal-status-derived lock** (no timed lease) — rejected: depends on the server\n  directly observing the agent process, which the hive cannot do across the network.\n- **Distributed lock service (etcd/Consul)** — rejected: heavy new dependency; a Postgres CAS + fencing\n  token meets the guarantee within the existing store.","lineStart":1,"lineEnd":70,"totalLines":70,"truncated":false}},"title":"dev-docs/adr/0009-lease-checkout-fencing.md","time":{"start":1782856867658,"end":1782856867664}},"id":"prt_f1a8cdf47001NSiOaGHtvfc2Sv","sessionID":"ses_0e57366b4ffeVAMRD3KZD8mtXC","messageID":"msg_f1a8cd83d002UO76lBsfqVTETd"}}
{"type":"tool_use","timestamp":1782856867807,"sessionID":"ses_0e57366b4ffeVAMRD3KZD8mtXC","part":{"type":"tool","tool":"read","callID":"call_9orgb9p8","state":{"status":"completed","input":{"filePath":"/home/david/Code/vk-swarm/.claude/worktrees/bridge-cse_01B8B52jjMEdikaLRoA25qhr/dev-docs/adr/0010-task-status-state-machine.md"},"output":"<path>/home/david/Code/vk-swarm/.claude/worktrees/bridge-cse_01B8B52jjMEdikaLRoA25qhr/dev-docs/adr/0010-task-status-state-machine.md</path>\n<type>file</type>\n<content>\n1: # ADR-0010 — Explicit task.status state machine with single-author transitions\n2: \n3: - **Status:** accepted\n4: - **Date:** 2026-06-30\n5: - **Workstream:** vk-swarm-hive-redesign\n6: - **Supersedes behaviour of:** field-level last-write-wins on `task.status`\n7:   (`upsert_from_node`/`upsert_remote_task`)\n8: \n9: ## Context\n10: \n11: Today `task.status` is reconciled field-by-field with no explicit transition model: the hive's\n12: `upsert_from_node` stamps a monotonic delivery counter and last-write-wins (analysis §2.4), and the node\n13: accepts hive status via the `remote_version`-only gate that silently clobbers concurrent local edits\n14: (`task/sync.rs:300`, `task/queries.rs:305-307`). There is **no agreement on who may author which\n15: transition**.\n16: \n17: Two concrete hazards confirmed in code:\n18: \n19: - **Status enum value drift** — SQLite stores `inprogress`/`inreview`; Postgres stores the hyphenated\n20:   enum `in-progress`/`in-review` (agent-C schema diff). Any path that doesn't map is a silent-corruption\n21:   risk.\n22: - Paperclip demonstrates the pattern worth copying is its **plugin-lifecycle `VALID_TRANSITIONS` map**\n23:   (`paperclip/plugin-lifecycle.ts:79-93`), **not** its ad-hoc issue path whose `assertTransition` only\n24:   rejects *unknown* statuses (`issues.ts:109`).\n25: \n26: ## Decision\n27: \n28: Define `task.status` as an **explicit guarded transition matrix** where **every transition has exactly\n29: one authoritative author** (SC4).\n30: \n31: **Reconciliation with the real enum (ratified 2026-06-30).** `task.status` is exactly\n32: `{Todo, InProgress, InReview, Done, Cancelled}` in both crates (`crates/db/src/models/task/mod.rs:27`,\n33: `crates/remote/src/db/tasks.rs:25`) — there is **no `Assigned` and no `Failed` variant**. SC4's\n34: parenthetical `assigned`/`failed` are **authority labels for lifecycle concepts, not `task.status`\n35: values**, and map to other columns:\n36: - **`assigned`** = the existence of an **active `node_task_assignments` row** (hive-authored, the\n37:   assignment layer — ADR-0009), NOT a `task.status` value.\n38: - **`failed`** = an **`execution_status`** outcome on the assignment / execution process (node-reported,\n39:   the execution layer), NOT a `task.status` value.\n40: \n41: The `task.status` matrix over the real enum:\n42: \n43: | Transition | Author |\n44: |---|---|\n45: | `todo → in-progress` | **hive** (on assignment + node start) |\n46: | `in-progress → in-review` | **node** (run completed, awaiting review) |\n47: | `in-progress → done` | **node** (terminal) |\n48: | `in-review → done` / `in-review → in-progress` (reopen) | **hive** (operator review) |\n49: | `* → cancelled` | **hive** (operator action) |\n50: \n51: (The \"assigned\" milestone is the `node_task_assignments` row created by the hive's atomic checkout,\n52: ADR-0009; the \"failed\" outcome is the assignment/execution `execution_status`. Both are single-author\n53: in their own layer, so the no-field-level-conflict guarantee holds across all three surfaces.)\n54: \n55: - A **node-reported** transition is accepted by the hive only when carried by a valid lease + current\n56:   fencing token ([ADR-0009](./0009-lease-checkout-fencing.md)); illegal transitions are rejected, not\n57:   merged. Because each transition has a single author, there is **no field-level status conflict**\n58:   (SC4).\n59: - **One canonical wire representation** for the status value resolves the `inprogress`/`in-progress`\n60:   drift; the node and hive serialize identically (the mapping is applied once, at the boundary).\n61: \n62: ## Consequences\n63: \n64: - Removes the last-write-wins status race and the silent-clobber window for status specifically;\n65:   combined with [ADR-0007](./0007-single-inbound-channel-one-delete-one-conflict.md)'s dirty-guard,\n66:   status is never lost.\n67: - Canonicalizing the enum value is a wire-format/representation change touching both schemas\n68:   (irreversible; covered in the [ADR-0011](./0011-hive-only-state-cutover.md) cutover mapping).\n69: - The matrix is the contract P5 (dependency/priority) and P6 (management agent) build on.\n70: \n71: ## Alternatives considered\n72: \n73: - **Keep last-write-wins, add a status-only conflict resolver** — rejected: still a merge of a field\n74:   two parties write; the state machine removes the conflict at the source.\n75: - **Single global status enum shared verbatim** — desirable but out of scope; this ADR fixes the\n76:   *value representation* mismatch without consolidating the two schema definitions (hygiene, deferred).\n\n(End of file - total 76 lines)\n</content>","metadata":{"preview":"# ADR-0010 — Explicit task.status state machine with single-author transitions\n\n- **Status:** accepted\n- **Date:** 2026-06-30\n- **Workstream:** vk-swarm-hive-redesign\n- **Supersedes behaviour of:** field-level last-write-wins on `task.status`\n  (`upsert_from_node`/`upsert_remote_task`)\n\n## Context\n\nToday `task.status` is reconciled field-by-field with no explicit transition model: the hive's\n`upsert_from_node` stamps a monotonic delivery counter and last-write-wins (analysis §2.4), and the node\naccepts hive status via the `remote_version`-only gate that silently clobbers concurrent local edits\n(`task/sync.rs:300`, `task/queries.rs:305-307`). There is **no agreement on who may author which\ntransition**.\n\nTwo concrete hazards confirmed in code:\n\n- **Status enum value drift** — SQLite stores `inprogress`/`inreview`; Postgres stores the hyphenated\n  enum `in-progress`/`in-review` (agent-C schema diff). Any path that doesn't map is a silent-corruption","truncated":false,"loaded":[],"display":{"type":"file","path":"/home/david/Code/vk-swarm/.claude/worktrees/bridge-cse_01B8B52jjMEdikaLRoA25qhr/dev-docs/adr/0010-task-status-state-machine.md","text":"# ADR-0010 — Explicit task.status state machine with single-author transitions\n\n- **Status:** accepted\n- **Date:** 2026-06-30\n- **Workstream:** vk-swarm-hive-redesign\n- **Supersedes behaviour of:** field-level last-write-wins on `task.status`\n  (`upsert_from_node`/`upsert_remote_task`)\n\n## Context\n\nToday `task.status` is reconciled field-by-field with no explicit transition model: the hive's\n`upsert_from_node` stamps a monotonic delivery counter and last-write-wins (analysis §2.4), and the node\naccepts hive status via the `remote_version`-only gate that silently clobbers concurrent local edits\n(`task/sync.rs:300`, `task/queries.rs:305-307`). There is **no agreement on who may author which\ntransition**.\n\nTwo concrete hazards confirmed in code:\n\n- **Status enum value drift** — SQLite stores `inprogress`/`inreview`; Postgres stores the hyphenated\n  enum `in-progress`/`in-review` (agent-C schema diff). Any path that doesn't map is a silent-corruption\n  risk.\n- Paperclip demonstrates the pattern worth copying is its **plugin-lifecycle `VALID_TRANSITIONS` map**\n  (`paperclip/plugin-lifecycle.ts:79-93`), **not** its ad-hoc issue path whose `assertTransition` only\n  rejects *unknown* statuses (`issues.ts:109`).\n\n## Decision\n\nDefine `task.status` as an **explicit guarded transition matrix** where **every transition has exactly\none authoritative author** (SC4).\n\n**Reconciliation with the real enum (ratified 2026-06-30).** `task.status` is exactly\n`{Todo, InProgress, InReview, Done, Cancelled}` in both crates (`crates/db/src/models/task/mod.rs:27`,\n`crates/remote/src/db/tasks.rs:25`) — there is **no `Assigned` and no `Failed` variant**. SC4's\nparenthetical `assigned`/`failed` are **authority labels for lifecycle concepts, not `task.status`\nvalues**, and map to other columns:\n- **`assigned`** = the existence of an **active `node_task_assignments` row** (hive-authored, the\n  assignment layer — ADR-0009), NOT a `task.status` value.\n- **`failed`** = an **`execution_status`** outcome on the assignment / execution process (node-reported,\n  the execution layer), NOT a `task.status` value.\n\nThe `task.status` matrix over the real enum:\n\n| Transition | Author |\n|---|---|\n| `todo → in-progress` | **hive** (on assignment + node start) |\n| `in-progress → in-review` | **node** (run completed, awaiting review) |\n| `in-progress → done` | **node** (terminal) |\n| `in-review → done` / `in-review → in-progress` (reopen) | **hive** (operator review) |\n| `* → cancelled` | **hive** (operator action) |\n\n(The \"assigned\" milestone is the `node_task_assignments` row created by the hive's atomic checkout,\nADR-0009; the \"failed\" outcome is the assignment/execution `execution_status`. Both are single-author\nin their own layer, so the no-field-level-conflict guarantee holds across all three surfaces.)\n\n- A **node-reported** transition is accepted by the hive only when carried by a valid lease + current\n  fencing token ([ADR-0009](./0009-lease-checkout-fencing.md)); illegal transitions are rejected, not\n  merged. Because each transition has a single author, there is **no field-level status conflict**\n  (SC4).\n- **One canonical wire representation** for the status value resolves the `inprogress`/`in-progress`\n  drift; the node and hive serialize identically (the mapping is applied once, at the boundary).\n\n## Consequences\n\n- Removes the last-write-wins status race and the silent-clobber window for status specifically;\n  combined with [ADR-0007](./0007-single-inbound-channel-one-delete-one-conflict.md)'s dirty-guard,\n  status is never lost.\n- Canonicalizing the enum value is a wire-format/representation change touching both schemas\n  (irreversible; covered in the [ADR-0011](./0011-hive-only-state-cutover.md) cutover mapping).\n- The matrix is the contract P5 (dependency/priority) and P6 (management agent) build on.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- **Keep last-write-wins, add a status-only conflict resolver** — rejected: still a merge of a field\n  two parties write; the state machine removes the conflict at the source.\n- **Single global status enum shared verbatim** — desirable but out of scope; this ADR fixes the\n  *value representation* mismatch without consolidating the two schema definitions (hygiene, deferred).","lineStart":1,"lineEnd":76,"totalLines":76,"truncated":false}},"title":"dev-docs/adr/0010-task-status-state-machine.md","time":{"start":1782856867800,"end":1782856867805}},"id":"prt_f1a8cdfd50017y4nQ1w6aP8M7v","sessionID":"ses_0e57366b4ffeVAMRD3KZD8mtXC","messageID":"msg_f1a8cd83d002UO76lBsfqVTETd"}}

The `shared_tasks` write feeds the **REST bulk snapshot**\n16:   reconcile (`node_runner.rs:986` → `RemoteClient::fetch_bulk_snapshot`, `remote_client.rs:752` →\n17:   `Task::upsert_remote_task`, `node_runner.rs:1012`); the activity row feeds the **WS activity stream**\n18:   (`project_watcher_task` → `ActivityProcessor::process_event`, `processor.rs:57`). Both run\n19:   continuously, so one change double-delivers.\n20: - **The `ElectricTaskSyncService` task-shape poll is dead** — `sync_project_tasks`\n21:   (`electric_task_sync.rs:164`) has zero runtime callers; the frontend Electric collections subscribe\n22:   only to `nodes`/`projects`/`node_projects` shapes, not `shared_tasks` (`collections.ts:82,99,116`).\n23: - **Updates are idempotent** (all three apply sites funnel through `upsert_remote_task` with the gate\n24:   `WHERE excluded.remote_version > tasks.remote_version OR tasks.remote_version IS NULL`,\n25:   `task/sync.rs:300`), **but DELETE diverges**: bulk-snapshot reconcile **hard-deletes** the local row\n26:   (`Task::delete_by_shared_task_id`, `node_runner.rs:1034`, `task/sync.rs:370`) while the WS\n27:   `task.deleted` path only **soft-unlinks** (`Task::set_shared_task_id(.., None)`, `processor.rs:437`).\n28:   For the **same** hive soft-delete (`shared_tasks.deleted_at = NOW()`, `remote/src/db/tasks.rs:1122`),\n29:   the node's outcome depends on which channel wins the race.\n30: - **`task.reassigned` is dropped** by the activity processor (`processor.rs:77` `_ =>` arm), so\n31:   reassignment only lands via the bulk snapshot — a hard channel dependency.\n32: - **Local edits are silently clobbered:** the inbound gate is `remote_version`-only and the local\n33:   update path does **not** bump `remote_version` (`task/queries.rs:305-307`), so an arriving hive\n34:   `version = N+1` overwrites a concurrent local edit with no dirty-flag or merge.\n35: \n36: This is the §2.7 \"broadcast fan-out double-delivery\" item resolved in code (analysis §2.7).\n37: \n38: ## Decision\n39: \n40: 1. **One live inbound channel.** The **WS activity stream is the single live delivery path**. The REST\n41:    bulk snapshot is demoted to a **cold-start / gap-fill reconcile** only — it never runs as a second\n42:    continuous channel alongside the WS stream. The dead `ElectricTaskSyncService` task-shape path is\n43:    removed.\n44: 2. **One delete semantic.** A hive soft-delete maps to **soft-unlink + tombstone on the node**\n45:    (clear `shared_task_id`, retain local `task_attempt`/run artifacts), applied **identically** on the\n46:    live channel and the reconcile. The hub owns the board; the node never loses local work it ran.\n47: 3. **One conflict policy.** The hive is authoritative for shared-task fields; node-local edits travel\n48:    up the ordered outbox ([ADR-0008](./0008-node-hive-ordered-ack-outbox.md)). The node applies a\n49:    **dirty-guard**: an inbound update never overwrites a field that has an unacked outbound op. No\n50:    silent clobber; the `remote_version`-only gate is replaced.\n51: 4. **No dropped event types.** The single channel must handle `task.reassigned` (and every authored\n52:    event), closing the `processor.rs:77` gap.\n53: \n54: ## Consequences\n55: \n56: - Eliminates the non-deterministic delete and the double-delivery harm class (SC7); reassignment is no\n57:   longer channel-dependent.\n58: - The reconcile path is repurposed as the anti-entropy gap-fill ([ADR-0008](./0008-node-hive-ordered-ack-outbox.md), SC5),\n59:   not a parallel writer.\n60: - Removing the Electric task-shape code is a deletion (irreversible); the Electric proxy used by the\n61:   hive UI for `nodes`/`projects` shapes is untouched.\n62: \n63: ## Alternatives considered\n64: \n65: - **Keep both channels, dedup by version** — rejected: leaves the divergent DELETE and the dropped\n66:   `task.reassigned`, and the version gate cannot protect local edits.\n67: - **Make Electric the single channel** — rejected: it is dead on both the Rust node side and the\n68:   frontend; finishing it would re-introduce a third apply path.\n\n(End of file - total 68 lines)\n</content>","metadata":{"preview":"# ADR-0007 — Collapse hive→node delivery to one channel, one delete semantic, one conflict policy\n\n- **Status:** accepted\n- **Date:** 2026-06-30\n- **Workstream:** vk-swarm-hive-redesign\n- **Supersedes behaviour of:** the dual REST-bulk-snapshot + WS-activity inbound paths and the dead\n  `ElectricTaskSyncService` task-shape path\n\n## Context\n\nVerified in code (read-only investigation, file:line):\n\n- **Two live inbound channels deliver the same logical change.** A hive `update_task` writes\n  `shared_tasks` **and** inserts an activity row in one transaction\n  (`crates/remote/src/db/tasks.rs:892-893`). The `shared_tasks` write feeds the **REST bulk snapshot**\n  reconcile (`node_runner.rs:986` → `RemoteClient::fetch_bulk_snapshot`, `remote_client.rs:752` →\n  `Task::upsert_remote_task`, `node_runner.rs:1012`); the activity row feeds the **WS activity stream**\n  (`project_watcher_task` → `ActivityProcessor::process_event`, `processor.rs:57`). Both run\n  continuously, so one change double-delivers.\n- **The `ElectricTaskSyncService` task-shape poll is dead** — `sync_project_tasks`\n  (`electric_task_sync.rs:164`) has zero runtime callers; the frontend Electric collections subscribe\n  only to `nodes`/`projects`/`node_projects` shapes, not `shared_tasks` (`collections.ts:82,99,116`).\n- **Updates are idempotent** (all three apply sites funnel through `upsert_remote_task` with the gate\n  `WHERE excluded.remote_version > tasks.remote_version OR tasks.remote_version IS NULL`,\n  `task/sync.rs:300`), **but DELETE diverges**: bulk-snapshot reconcile **hard-deletes** the local row\n  (`Task::delete_by_shared_task_id`, `node_runner.rs:1034`, `task/sync.rs:370`) while the WS\n  `task.deleted` path only **soft-unlinks** (`Task::set_shared_task_id(.., None)`, `processor.rs:437`).\n  For the **same** hive soft-delete (`shared_tasks.deleted_at = NOW()`, `remote/src/db/tasks.rs:1122`),\n  the node's outcome depends on which channel wins the race.\n- **`task.reassigned` is dropped** by the activity processor (`processor.rs:77` `_ =>` arm), so\n  reassignment only lands via the bulk snapshot — a hard channel dependency.\n- **Local edits are silently clobbered:** the inbound gate is `remote_version`-only and the local\n  update path does **not** bump `remote_version` (`task/queries.rs:305-307`), so an arriving hive\n  `version = N+1` overwrites a concurrent local edit with no dirty-flag or merge.\n\nThis is the §2.7 \"broadcast fan-out double-delivery\" item resolved in code (analysis §2.7).\n\n## Decision\n\n1. **One live inbound channel.** The **WS activity stream is the single live delivery path**. The REST\n   bulk snapshot is demoted to a **cold-start / gap-fill reconcile** only — it never runs as a second\n   continuous channel alongside the WS stream. The dead `ElectricTaskSyncService` task-shape path is\n   removed.\n2. **One delete semantic.** A hive soft-delete maps to **soft-unlink + tombstone on the node**\n   (clear `shared_task_id`, retain local `task_attempt`/run artifacts), applied **identically** on the\n   live channel and the reconcile. The hub owns the board; the node never loses local work it ran.\n3. **One conflict policy.** The hive is authoritative for shared-task fields; node-local edits travel\n   up the ordered outbox ([ADR-0008](./0008-node-hive-ordered-ack-outbox.md)). The node applies a\n   **dirty-guard**: an inbound update never overwrites a field that has an unacked outbound op. No\n   silent clobber; the `remote_version`-only gate is replaced.\n4. **No dropped event types.** The single channel must handle `task.reassigned` (and every authored\n   event), closing the `processor.rs:77` gap.\n\n## Consequences\n\n- Eliminates the non-deterministic delete and the double-delivery harm class (SC7); reassignment is no\n  longer channel-dependent.\n- The reconcile path is repurposed as the anti-entropy gap-fill ([ADR-0008](./0008-node-hive-ordered-ack-outbox.md), SC5),\n  not a parallel writer.\n- Removing the Electric task-shape code is a deletion (irreversible); the Electric proxy used by the\n  hive UI for `nodes`/`projects` shapes is untouched.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- **Keep both channels, dedup by version** — rejected: leaves the divergent DELETE and the dropped\n  `task.reassigned`, and the version gate cannot protect local edits.\n- **Make Electric the single channel** — rejected: it is dead on both the Rust node side and the\n  frontend; finishing it would re-introduce a third apply path.","lineStart":1,"lineEnd":68,"totalLines":68,"truncated":false}},"title":"dev-docs/adr/0007-single-inbound-channel-one-delete-one-conflict.md","time":{"start":1782856867945,"end":1782856867949}},"id":"prt_f1a8ce066001ftPJ5fk7dSCQcQ","sessionID":"ses_0e57366b4ffeVAMRD3KZD8mtXC","messageID":"msg_f1a8cd83d002UO76lBsfqVTETd"}}
{"type":"tool_use","timestamp":1782856868106,"sessionID":"ses_0e57366b4ffeVAMRD3KZD8mtXC","part":{"type":"tool","tool":"read","callID":"call_acf0cgxz","state":{"status":"completed","input":{"filePath":"/home/david/Code/vk-swarm/.claude/worktrees/bridge-cse_01B8B52jjMEdikaLRoA25qhr/dev-docs/adr/0008-node-hive-ordered-ack-outbox.md"},"output":"<path>/home/david/Code/vk-swarm/.claude/worktrees/bridge-cse_01B8B52jjMEdikaLRoA25qhr/dev-docs/adr/0008-node-hive-ordered-ack-outbox.md</path>\n<type>file</type>\n<content>\n1: # ADR-0008 — Node→hive sync via a single ordered, acknowledged outbox / op-log\n2: \n3: - **Status:** accepted\n4: - **Date:** 2026-06-30\n5: - **Workstream:** vk-swarm-hive-redesign\n6: - **Supersedes behaviour of:** the five independent node→hive push paths in `hive_sync.rs` +\n7:   `share/publisher.rs`\n8: \n9: ## Context\n10: \n11: Verified in code (file:line):\n12: \n13: - The node has **five independent outbound push paths** — task link (WS `TaskSync`,\n14:   `hive_sync.rs:303`), attempt (WS `AttemptSync`, `:368`), execution process (WS `ExecutionSync`,\n15:   `:434`), logs (WS `LogsBatch`, `:562`), and the share-task **HTTP POST**\n16:   (`share/publisher.rs:109`). Four ride one `mpsc::channel(64)` outbox (`hive_client.rs:723`).\n17: - **Cross-entity ordering is already enforced declaratively** — attempt sync skips when the parent\n18:   task is unlinked (`hive_sync.rs:340-349`, the load-bearing `continue`); exec and log `find_unsynced`\n19:   carry SQL JOIN guards on the parent's `hive_synced_at` (`execution_process/sync.rs:22-23`,\n20:   `log_entry/sync.rs:26-27`). So ordering is *guardable*, not the defect.\n21: - **The defect is ack timing.** For attempts/execs/logs the dirty flag is cleared by\n22:   `mark_hive_synced_batch` **immediately after the mpsc enqueue** (`hive_sync.rs:380-382,446-448,574-577`),\n23:   while the socket write happens later with **no ack** (`hive_client.rs:890-895`). A crash or drop\n24:   between enqueue and durable hive receipt **permanently marks the entity synced** and it is never\n25:   retried (`find_unsynced` filters it out) → silent write loss (§2.6, §2.7).\n26: - **No monotonic seq/version on child entities** — only `TaskSyncMessage` carries a hardcoded\n27:   `version: 1` (`hive_sync.rs:289`); `AttemptSyncMessage`/`ExecutionSyncMessage`/`LogsBatchMessage`\n28:   carry none, and no `*SyncResponse` ack types exist.\n29: \n30: ## Decision\n31: \n32: Replace the five push paths with **one per-node append-only op-log** in node SQLite:\n33: \n34: ```text\n35: outbox(seq INTEGER PK AUTOINCREMENT,   -- per-node monotonic\n36:        op_type, entity_type, entity_id,\n37:        payload, idempotency_key UNIQUE, fencing_token,\n38:        created_at, acked_at NULL)\n39: ```\n40: \n41: - **Ordered, single channel (SC2a).** Ops are appended in causal order; the existing\n42:   task→attempt→exec→log dependency becomes explicit op ordering. The node streams ops in `seq` order\n43:   over the WS — one channel, FIFO.\n44: - **Parent-before-child by construction (SC2b).** The hive **parks** a child op whose parent op has not\n45:   yet been applied and applies it once the parent lands; the node never emits a child before its\n46:   parent op.\n47: - **Acknowledged, no silent loss (SC2c).** The hive applies each op **idempotently**\n48:   (`idempotency_key` UNIQUE, `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`) and returns a **durable ack** carrying the\n49:   applied high-water `seq`. The node sets `acked_at` and advances its cursor **only on durable ack** —\n50:   the flag-clear-before-ack window is closed.\n51: - **Per-op monotonic version** replaces the hardcoded `version: 1`.\n52: - **Anti-entropy reconciliation (SC5)** rides this contract: on reconnect (and periodically) the node\n53:   re-streams from its unacked cursor, and a **digest exchange** (per-entity version/hash + outbox\n54:   high-water) detects silent divergence the cursor alone would miss; the hive replies with the ops/\n55:   pulls needed to heal. This *is* the replacement for the manual `reset_*` repair migrations — the\n56:   repurposed bulk-snapshot reconcile ([ADR-0007](./0007-single-inbound-channel-one-delete-one-conflict.md))\n57:   is its gap-fill leg.\n58: - An op **against a hive-assigned task** carries that task's current **fencing token**\n59:   ([ADR-0009](./0009-lease-checkout-fencing.md)) so stale-lease writes are rejected at apply.\n60:   Node-owned work (locally-created tasks + their attempts/execs/logs — the majority of ops) carries\n61:   **no token** and commits under the node's ownership identity, not a lease.\n62: \n63: ## Consequences\n64: \n65: - Closes the silent-write-loss window for attempts/execs/logs (SC2c) and guarantees cross-entity\n66:   ordering by construction (SC2b), not best-effort.\n67: - Deletes the four WS push paths and the HTTP share-publisher path as the sync mechanism (the share/\n68:   link operation becomes the task op at the head of the log). Irreversible wire-format + code deletion.\n69: - The op-log is the single event source later phases (P3/P6) consume.\n70: \n71: ## Alternatives considered\n72: \n73: - **Add acks to the existing five paths** (targeted bracket, analysis §2.6) — rejected: keeps five\n74:   parallel cursors, no single ordering guarantee, and the share path stays a separate transport. The\n75:   rebuild was decided at the program level (analysis §2.6); this ADR records the op-log realization.\n76: - **Vector clocks / CRDT merge** — rejected: the hub-and-spoke topology makes the hive authoritative,\n77:   so a per-node monotonic op-log with idempotency keys is sufficient and far simpler.\n\n(End of file - total 77 lines)\n</content>","metadata":{"preview":"# ADR-0008 — Node→hive sync via a single ordered, acknowledged outbox / op-log\n\n- **Status:** accepted\n- **Date:** 2026-06-30\n- **Workstream:** vk-swarm-hive-redesign\n- **Supersedes behaviour of:** the five independent node→hive push paths in `hive_sync.rs` +\n  `share/publisher.rs`\n\n## Context\n\nVerified in code (file:line):\n\n- The node has **five independent outbound push paths** — task link (WS `TaskSync`,\n  `hive_sync.rs:303`), attempt (WS `AttemptSync`, `:368`), execution process (WS `ExecutionSync`,\n  `:434`), logs (WS `LogsBatch`, `:562`), and the share-task **HTTP POST**\n  (`share/publisher.rs:109`). Four ride one `mpsc::channel(64)` outbox (`hive_client.rs:723`).\n- **Cross-entity ordering is already enforced declaratively** — attempt sync skips when the parent\n  task is unlinked (`hive_sync.rs:340-349`, the load-bearing `continue`); exec and log `find_unsynced`\n  carry SQL JOIN guards on the parent's `hive_synced_at` (`execution_process/sync.rs:22-23`,\n  `log_entry/sync.rs:26-27`). Four ride one `mpsc::channel(64)` outbox (`hive_client.rs:723`).\n- **Cross-entity ordering is already enforced declaratively** — attempt sync skips when the parent\n  task is unlinked (`hive_sync.rs:340-349`, the load-bearing `continue`); exec and log `find_unsynced`\n  carry SQL JOIN guards on the parent's `hive_synced_at` (`execution_process/sync.rs:22-23`,\n  `log_entry/sync.rs:26-27`). So ordering is *guardable*, not the defect.\n- **The defect is ack timing.** For attempts/execs/logs the dirty flag is cleared by\n  `mark_hive_synced_batch` **immediately after the mpsc enqueue** (`hive_sync.rs:380-382,446-448,574-577`),\n  while the socket write happens later with **no ack** (`hive_client.rs:890-895`). A crash or drop\n  between enqueue and durable hive receipt **permanently marks the entity synced** and it is never\n  retried (`find_unsynced` filters it out) → silent write loss (§2.6, §2.7).\n- **No monotonic seq/version on child entities** — only `TaskSyncMessage` carries a hardcoded\n  `version: 1` (`hive_sync.rs:289`); `AttemptSyncMessage`/`ExecutionSyncMessage`/`LogsBatchMessage`\n  carry none, and no `*SyncResponse` ack types exist.\n\n## Decision\n\nReplace the five push paths with **one per-node append-only op-log** in node SQLite:\n\n```text\noutbox(seq INTEGER PK AUTOINCREMENT,   -- per-node monotonic\n       op_type, entity_type, entity_id,\n       payload, idempotency_key UNIQUE, fencing_token,\n       created_at, acked_at NULL)\n```\n\n- **Ordered, single channel (SC2a).** Ops are appended in causal order; the existing\n  task→attempt→exec→log dependency becomes explicit op ordering. The node streams ops in `seq` order\n  over the WS — one channel, FIFO.\n- **Parent-before-child by construction (SC2b).** The hive **parks** a child op whose parent op has not\n  yet been applied and applies it once the parent lands; the node never emits a child before its\n  parent op.\n- **Acknowledged, no silent loss (SC2c).** The hive applies each op **idempotently**\n  (`idempotency_key` UNIQUE, `ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING`) and returns a **durable ack** carrying the\n  applied high-water `seq`. The node sets `acked_at` and advances its cursor **only on durable ack** —\n  the flag-clear-before-ack window is closed.\n- **Per-op monotonic version** replaces the hardcoded `version: 1`.\n- **Anti-entropy reconciliation (SC5)** rides this contract: on reconnect (and periodically) the node\n  re-streams from its unacked cursor, and a **digest exchange** (per-entity version/hash + outbox\n  high-water) detects silent divergence the cursor alone would miss; the hive replies with the ops/\n  pulls needed to heal. This *is* the replacement for the manual `reset_*` repair migrations — the\n  repurposed bulk-snapshot reconcile ([ADR-0007](./0007-single-inbound-channel-one-delete-one-conflict.md))\n  is its gap-fill leg.\n- An op **against a hive-assigned task** carries that task's current **fencing token**\n  ([ADR-0009](./0009-lease-checkout-fencing.md)) so stale-lease writes are rejected at apply.\n  Node-owned work (locally-created tasks + their attempts/execs/logs — the majority of ops) carries\n  **no token** and commits under the node's ownership identity, not a lease.\n\n## Consequences\n\n- Closes the silent-write-loss window for attempts/execs/logs (SC2c) and guarantees cross-entity\n  ordering by construction (SC2b), not best-effort.\n- Deletes the four WS push paths and the HTTP share-publisher path as the sync mechanism (the share/\n  link operation becomes the task op at the head of the log). Irreversible wire-format + code deletion.\n- The op-log is the single event source later phases (P3/P6) consume.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- **Add acks to the existing five paths** (targeted bracket, analysis §2.6) — rejected: keeps five\n  parallel cursors, no single ordering guarantee, and the share path stays a separate transport. The\n  rebuild was decided at the program level (analysis §2.6); this ADR records the op-log realization.\n- **Vector clocks / CRDT merge** — rejected: the hub-and-spoke topology makes the hive authoritative,\n  so a per-node monotonic op-log with idempotency keys is sufficient and far simpler.","lineStart":1,"lineEnd":77,"totalLines":77,"truncated":false}},"title":"dev-docs/adr/0008-node-hive-ordered-ack-outbox.md","time":{"start":1782856868090,"end":1782856868101}},"id":"prt_f1a8ce0f7001l5kIEl4ZFeV6h5","sessionID":"ses_0e57366b4ffeVAMRD3KZD8mtXC","messageID":"msg_f1a8cd83d002UO76lBsfqVTETd"}}

Two facts\nshape the cutover:\n\n- **The node↔hive id spaces differ** — node `tasks.id` ≠ hive `shared_tasks.id`, bridged by\n  `tasks.shared_task_id` ↔ `shared_tasks.source_task_id`/`source_node_id`. This bridge **must** be\n  preserved or every existing link breaks.\n- **There is no board-ordering/layout table** — kanban order is *derived* from `status` + `activity_at`\n  (grep for board/column/position/rank returns only comments). So there is **no operator-entered layout\n  to migrate** — a real scope reduction.\n\n## Decision\n\nClassify all hive-only state into three buckets and cut over accordingly:\n\n**MUST-MIGRATE** (one-time data migration into the rebuilt hive, before cutover):\n\n- `node_api_keys` — operator-issued M2M credentials; **irrecoverable** (loss forces re-keying every node).\n- `nodes` — node registry/identity (machine_id, public_url, key bindings depend on it).\n- `node_task_assignments` (active, `completed_at IS NULL`) — the only record of which node owns which\n  in-flight task.\n- `swarm_projects` + `swarm_project_nodes` — operator-defined project↔node linking topology (incl.\n  `is_owner`).\n- `swarm_templates` — operator-authored, org-global.\n- `shared_tasks` — the task registry incl. hive-only attribution (`creator_user_id`, `assignee_user_id`,\n  `deleted_by_user_id`/`deleted_at`, `owner_node_id`/`executing_node_id`) **and the node↔hive id\n  bridge** (`source_task_id`/`source_node_id`). **Apply the status enum value mapping**\n  ([ADR-0010](./0010-task-status-state-machine.md)) on re-import.\n- `labels` + `shared_task_labels` — hive-created labels and all task↔label assignments.\n- Identity/tenancy — `users`, `organizations`, `organization_member_metadata`,\n  `organization_invitations`, `oauth_accounts`.\n\n**REGENERABLE** (drop and rebuild from node re-ingest via the new outbox,\n[ADR-0008](./0008-node-hive-ordered-ack-outbox.md)):\n\n- `node_local_projects`, `node_execution_processes`, `node_task_output_logs`,\n  `node_task_progress_events`, attempt `sync_state`/`backfill_request_id`/`last_full_sync_at`,\n  `project_activity_counters`, Electric replication plumbing.\n\n**DISCARDABLE** (not migrated):\n\n- `activity` history feed, `auth_sessions`, `oauth_handoffs`, `revoked_refresh_tokens`, completed\n  `node_task_assignments`.\n\n**Cutover sequence.** Because `vk-swarm-node-foundations` already made nodes authoritative for their own\nstate, cutover is: (1) run the one-time MUST-MIGRATE migration into the rebuilt hive, preserving the id\nbridge; (2) bring nodes online — they re-ingest REGENERABLE state via the outbox; (3) discard the\ndiscardable tables.\n\n## Consequences\n\n- SC6 is satisfied with an evidence-backed inventory; the rebuild cannot silently lose operator state.\n- Dropping REGENERABLE/DISCARDABLE tables and remapping status values are irreversible data operations —\n  gated behind a pre-cutover backup.\n- The \"no board-ordering table\" finding removes a feared migration entirely.\n\n## Alternatives considered\n\n- **Migrate everything wholesale** — rejected: drags transient sync bookkeeping and stale history into\n  the rebuilt schema, defeating the point of the rebuild.\n- **Rebuild empty and let nodes repopulate everything** — rejected: loses the irrecoverable\n  operator-only state (API keys, swarm-project topology, templates, identity, attribution).","lineStart":1,"lineEnd":73,"totalLines":73,"truncated":false}},"title":"dev-docs/adr/0011-hive-only-state-cutover.md","time":{"start":1782856868219,"end":1782856868223}},"id":"prt_f1a8ce1780015jZygS70OthN8S","sessionID":"ses_0e57366b4ffeVAMRD3KZD8mtXC","messageID":"msg_f1a8cd83d002UO76lBsfqVTETd"}}
