(create).\n- **Before:** (file does not exist)\n- **After:** a self-contained module encoding ADR-0010 §D over the hive `TaskStatus`\n  (`crate::db::tasks::TaskStatus` — `Todo/InProgress/InReview/Done/Cancelled`, `tasks.rs:25`). It declares\n  WHO authors each transition; it does NOT touch the DB, lease, or fencing.\n```rust\n//! Explicit `task.status` transition matrix (ADR-0010 §D, CONTRACT §D).\n//!\n//! Single source of truth for WHICH party may author WHICH status transition. Every legal\n//! transition has exactly ONE authoritative author, so there is no field-level status merge (SC4).\n//! This module is pure: it encodes the matrix and answers author/legality questions. Enforcement at\n//! the apply site (rejecting an illegal or wrong-author transition, and requiring a valid\n//! lease + fencing token for node-reported transitions) lives in `session.rs::handle_op_batch`\n//! (task 303), which rides P2's fencing check (CONTRACT §C).\n\nuse crate::db::tasks::TaskStatus;\n\n/// The party authorized to author a given status transition.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq)]\npub(crate) enum TransitionAuthor {\n    /// Hive-authored (operator / assignment lifecycle): `todo→in-progress` (the on-assign-and-start\n    /// analog), `in-review→done` / `in-review→in-progress` (operator review), `*→cancelled`. (ADR-0010's\n    /// reconciled matrix collapses the `assigned` concept into the `node_task_assignments` row, not a\n    /// hive `TaskStatus` value — see the module/STOP note.)\n    Hive,\n    /// Node-reported up the outbox, accepted only with a valid lease + current fencing token (303):\n    /// `in-progress→done`, `in-progress→in-review`.\n    Node,\n}\n\n/// Return the sole authoritative author of `from → to`, or `None` if the transition is illegal\n/// (not in the matrix). A no-op (`from == to`) returns `None` — it is not an authored transition.\npub(crate) fn author_of_transition(from: TaskStatus, to: TaskStatus) -> Option<TransitionAuthor> {\n    use TaskStatus::*;\n    match (from, to) {\n        // hive-authored lifecycle\n        (Todo, InProgress) => Some(TransitionAuthor::Hive), // assign + start\n        (InReview, InProgress) => Some(TransitionAuthor::Hive), // operator reopen\n        (InReview, Done) => Some(TransitionAuthor::Hive), // operator approve\n        (_, Cancelled) if from != Cancelled => Some(TransitionAuthor::Hive),\n        // node-reported work/terminal transitions\n        (InProgress, Done) => Some(TransitionAuthor::Node),\n        (InProgress, InReview) => Some(TransitionAuthor::Node),\n        // everything else (incl. no-ops) is illegal\n        _ => None,\n    }\n}\n\n/// True iff a NODE report may author `from → to` (the predicate 303's enforcement calls before\n/// applying a node-reported status). False for hive-authored transitions, illegal transitions, and\n/// no-ops.\npub(crate) fn node_may_author(from: TaskStatus, to: TaskStatus) -> bool {\n    matches!(author_of_transition(from, to), Some(TransitionAuthor::Node))\n}\n```\n- **File:** `crates/remote/src/nodes/ws/mod.rs`\n- **Anchor:** the module-declaration block (`ws/mod.rs:16-19`).\n- **Before:**\n```rust\nmod connection;\nmod dispatcher;\npub mod message;\nmod session;\n```\n- **After:**\n```rust\nmod connection;\nmod dispatcher;\npub mod message;\nmod session;\nmod status_machine;\n```\n\n## Allowed moves\nONLY: create `status_machine.rs` with the enum + the two fns + the colocated `#[cfg(test)] mod tests`,\nand add the single `mod status_machine;` line to `ws/mod.rs`. Do NOT touch `session.rs`, the WS enum\ndefinitions, the node crate, any migration, or `tasks.rs`. Do NOT add the enforcement/DB/lease logic\nhere — that is 303. The matrix is data only.\n\n## STOP triggers\n- The hive `TaskStatus` enum (`crate::db::tasks::TaskStatus`, `tasks.rs:25`) has **no `Assigned`\n  variant** — `Todo/InProgress/InReview/Done/Cancelled` only. Two legacy-path interactions are now resolved\nunder it: (1) the legacy execution-status map never produces `Done` (`Completed→InReview`,\n`session.rs:672`), so the only node-authorable apply the legacy path can make is `InProgress→InReview` —\nthe accept test seeds `in-progress`, reports `Completed`, and asserts the result is `in-review` (a\nnode-authored transition). (2) The map produces `Running→InProgress`, but `InProgress` is never a\nnode-authorable TARGET (the hive owns `Todo→InProgress` \"on assignment + node start\" and the\n`InReview→InProgress` reopen). So a node `Running` report is correctly a **no-op** once the hive has\nalready moved the task to `in-progress`, and is correctly **rejected** if the task is still in its initial\nstate — the hive, not the node, authors the start. This is intended; no special case. See\n`dev-docs/adr/0010-task-status-state-machine.md` (## Decision) and 301's reconciled matrix.\n\n## Failing test (write first)\n**WHY THIS TASK EXISTS (advisor §3 — surfaced, do NOT silently leave open):** there are TWO sites that\nwrite `shared_tasks.status` from a node. 303 guards the canonical op-log path (`handle_op_batch`). The\nSECOND is the LEGACY `handle_task_status` (`session.rs:625`), reached by `NodeMessage::TaskStatus`\n(`session.rs:524`): it maps `TaskExecutionStatus` → `TaskStatus` and calls\n`SharedTaskRepository::update_status_from_node` with NO author/lease/fencing context — pure last-write-wins,\nexactly the silent-clobber ADR-0010 removes. If this path is left ungated while we claim \"SC4 — no\nfield-level status conflict closed\", it is a hole. Two legacy-path interactions are now resolved\nunder it: (1) the legacy execution-status map never produces `Done` (`Completed→InReview`,\n`session.rs:672`), so the only node-authorable apply the legacy path can make is `InProgress→InReview` —\nthe accept test seeds `in-progress`, reports `Completed`, and asserts the result is `in-review` (a\nnode-authored transition). (2) The map produces `Running→InProgress`, but `InProgress` is never a\nnode-authorable TARGET (the hive owns `Todo→InProgress` \"on assignment + node start\" and the\n`InReview→InProgress` reopen). So a node `Running` report is correctly a **no-op** once the hive has\nalready moved the task to `in-progress`, and is correctly **rejected** if the task is still in its initial\nstate — the hive, not the node, authors the start. This is intended; no special case. The\nSECOND is the LEGACY `handle_task_status` (`session.rs:625`), reached by `NodeMessage::TaskStatus`\n(`session.rs:524`): it maps `TaskExecutionStatus` → `TaskStatus` and calls\n`SharedTaskRepository::update_status_from_node` with NO author/lease/fencing context — pure last-write-wins,\nexactly the silent-clobber ADR-0010 removes. The WS leg's existing \"soft-unlink\" (`processor.rs:437` `set_shared_task_id(.., None)`) is a **no-op\n   for a LINKED row**: its `WHERE … AND (shared_task_id IS NULL OR shared_task_id = $2) …` with `$2 =\n   NULL` reduces (SQLite three-valued logic, `= NULL` is never true) to `shared_task_id IS NULL`, so a\n   row that IS linked (`shared_task_id = S`) matches 0 rows and is never cleared. Verified empirically:\n   `UPDATE t SET s=NULL WHERE id=1 AND (s IS NULL OR s=NULL) …` leaves `s='S'`.\n\nSo today neither leg reliably soft-unlinks. The fix routes **BOTH legs through ONE working,\nexecutor-generic `unlink_by_shared_task_id`** — \"applied identically on both legs\" by construction\n(ADR-0007 §2). local_id).await.unwrap();\n        assert!(still.is_some(), \"local row is RETAINED (soft-unlink, not hard-delete)\");\n        assert!(still.unwrap().shared_task_id.is_none(), \"shared_task_id cleared (tombstone)\");\n    }\n\n    #[tokio::test]\n    async fn unlink_stale_shared_tasks_keeps_local_rows() {\n        let (pool, _temp_dir) = setup_test_pool().await;\n        let project_id = Uuid::new_v4();\n        let project_data = CreateProject {\n            name: \"Test Project\".to_string(),\n            git_repo_path: format!(\"/tmp/test-repo-{}\", project_id),\n            use_existing_repo: true,\n            clone_url: None,\n            setup_script: None,\n            dev_script: None,\n            cleanup_script: None,\n            copy_files: None,\n        };\n        Project::create(&pool, &project_data, project_id).await.unwrap();\n\n        let kept = Uuid::new_v4();\n        let stale = Uuid::new_v4();\n        let kept_shared = Uuid::new_v4();\n        let stale_shared = Uuid::new_v4();\n        for (lid, sid) in [(kept, kept_shared), (stale, stale_shared)] {\n            Task::create(&pool, &CreateTask::from_title_description(project_id, `kept_shared`; `stale_shared` is no longer present on hive.\n        let n = Task::unlink_stale_shared_tasks(&pool, project_id, &[kept_shared]).await.unwrap();\n        assert_eq!(n, 1, \"only the stale).await.unwrap().is_some(), \"stale local row retained\");\n    }\n```\n> `Task::find_by_id` lives in `task/queries.rs:166` (same `impl Task`, signature `(pool, id)`). The test\n> block already has all needed imports — add NO new `use` lines.\n\n## Change\n\n### 1. `crates/db/src/models/task/sync.rs` — add two soft-unlink helpers\n- **File:** `crates/db/src/models/task/sync.rs`\n- **Anchor:** the existing hard-delete helpers `delete_by_shared_task_id` (~L367) and\n  `delete_stale_shared_tasks` (~L385). **Do NOT remove them** — this task only ADDS the soft-unlink\n  variants; the reconcile leg switches to them in change #2. Place the two new fns immediately AFTER\n  `delete_stale_shared_tasks`'s closing `}` (~L416), before the `clear_orphaned_shared_task_ids` doc\n  comment. The new SQL mirrors the existing `clear_orphaned_shared_task_ids` pattern in the SAME file\n  (`SET shared_task_id = NULL, updated_at = CURRENT_TIMESTAMP`).\n- **Before (the boundary right after `delete_stale_shared_tasks`'s closing brace):**\n```rust\n        let result = query_builder.execute(pool).await?;\n        Ok(result.rows_affected())\n    }\n\n    /// Clear shared_task_id for orphaned tasks.\n```\n- **After:**\n```rust\n        let result = query_builder.execute(pool).await?;\n        Ok(result.rows_affected())\n    }\n\n    /// Soft-unlink a task from a deleted hive shared task (ADR-0007 one-delete semantic).\n    ///\n    /// Clears `shared_task_id` (tombstone) but RETAINS the local row and its `task_attempt`/run\n    /// artifacts — the hub owns the board, the node never loses local work it ran. This is the\n    /// SINGLE soft-unlink used by BOTH inbound legs — the WS `task.deleted` path (`processor.rs`, via a\n    /// `&mut Transaction`) AND the cold-start/gap-fill reconcile (`node_runner.rs`, via a `&SqlitePool`) —\n    /// so a hive soft-delete yields ONE node outcome regardless of which leg applies it. Executor-generic\n    /// (mirrors `set_shared_task_id`) so the tx-based caller can pass `tx.as_mut()`.\n    /// Returns the number of rows unlinked.\n    pub async fn unlink_by_shared_task_id<'e, E>(\n        executor: E,\n        shared_task_id: Uuid,\n    ) -> Result<u64, sqlx::Error>\n    where\n        E: Executor<'e, Database = Sqlite>,\n    {\n        let result = sqlx::query!(\n            r#\"UPDATE tasks\n               SET shared_task_id = NULL, updated_at = CURRENT_TIMESTAMP\n               WHERE shared_task_id = ?\"#,\n            shared_task_id\n        )\n        .execute(executor)\n        .await?;\n        Ok(result.rows_affected())\n    }\n\n    /// Soft-unlink shared tasks no longer present in the reconcile snapshot (ADR-0007).\n    ///\n    /// The stale-sweep analogue of `unlink_by_shared_task_id`: any task in this project whose\n    /// `shared_task_id` is NOT in the active set is unlinked (cleared) rather than hard-deleted,\n    /// preserving local attempts. Only touches rows that HAVE a `shared_task_id` (hive-synced),\n    /// leaving locally-created tasks untouched. Returns the number of rows unlinked.\n    pub async fn unlink_stale_shared_tasks(\n        pool: &SqlitePool,\n        project_id: Uuid,\n        active_shared_task_ids: &[Uuid],\n    ) -> Result<u64, sqlx::Error> {\n        if active_shared_task_ids.is_empty() {\n            return Ok(0);\n        }\n\n        let placeholders: Vec<String> = active_shared_task_ids\n            .iter()\n            .enumerate()\n            .map(|(i, _)| format!(\"${}\", i + 2))\n            .collect();\n        let placeholders_str = placeholders.join(\", \");\n\n        let query = format!(\n            r#\"UPDATE tasks\n               SET shared_task_id = NULL, updated_at = CURRENT_TIMESTAMP\n               WHERE project_id = $1\n               AND shared_task_id IS NOT NULL\n               AND shared_task_id NOT IN ({})\"#,\n            placeholders_str\n        );\n\n        let mut query_builder = sqlx::query(&query).bind(project_id);\n        for id in active_shared_task_ids {\n            query_builder = query_builder.bind(id);\n        }\n\n        let result = query_builder.execute(pool).await?;\n        Ok(result.rows_affected())\n    }\n\n    /// Clear shared_task_id for orphaned tasks.\n```\n\n### 2. `crates/services/src/services/node_runner.rs` — reconcile leg calls soft-unlink\n- **File:** `crates/services/src/services/node_runner.rs`\n- **Anchor:** The current\n  code finds the local task by `shared_task_id` then calls `set_shared_task_id(.., None)` BY LOCAL ID —\n  which (bug above) is a no-op for a linked row. Replace the whole find-then-clear dance with one\n  `unlink_by_shared_task_id` call keyed on the HIVE id, identical to the reconcile leg.\n- **Before:**\n```rust\n        // Find local task by shared_task_id and unlink it\n        if let Some(existing) = Task::find_by_shared_task_id(tx.as_mut(), hive_task.id).await? {\n            // Clear the shared_task_id to unlink from Hive\n            // We don't delete the local task - just unlink it\n            Task::set_shared_task_id(tx.as_mut(), existing.id, None).await?;\n\n            debug!(\n                local_task_id = %existing.id,\n                shared_task_id = %hive_task.id,\n                \"Unlinked local task from deleted Hive task\"\n            );\n        }\n```\n- **After:**\n```rust\n        // Soft-unlink via the SAME helper the reconcile leg uses (ADR-0007 one delete semantic):\n        // clear shared_task_id, keep the local row + its task_attempt. The connect-time reconcile leg **hard-deletes** the row\n   (`Task::delete_by_shared_task_id` + `delete_stale_shared_tasks`, `node_runner.rs:1034,1039`).\n2. The WS leg's existing \"soft-unlink\" (`processor.rs:437` `set_shared_task_id(.., None)`) is a **no-op\n   for a LINKED row**: its `WHERE … AND (shared_task_id IS NULL OR shared_task_id = $2) …` with `$2 =\n   NULL` reduces (SQLite three-valued logic, `= NULL` is never true) to `shared_task_id IS NULL`, so a\n   row that IS linked (`shared_task_id = S`) matches 0 rows and is never cleared. Verified empirically:\n   `UPDATE t SET s=NULL WHERE id=1 AND (s IS NULL OR s=NULL) …` leaves `s='S'`.\n\nSo today neither leg reliably soft-unlinks. The fix routes **BOTH legs through ONE working,\nexecutor-generic `unlink_by_shared_task_id`** — \"applied identically on both legs\" by construction\n(ADR-0007 §2). The new SQL mirrors the existing `clear_orphaned_shared_task_ids` pattern in the SAME file\n  (`SET shared_task_id = NULL, updated_at = CURRENT_TIMESTAMP`).\n- **Before (the boundary right after `delete_stale_shared_tasks`'s closing brace):**\n```rust\n        let result = query_builder.execute(pool).await?;\n        Ok(result.rows_affected())\n    }\n\n    /// Clear shared_task_id for orphaned tasks.\n```\n- **After:**\n```rust\n        let result = query_builder.execute(pool).await?;\n        Ok(result.rows_affected())\n    }\n\n    /// Soft-unlink a task from a deleted hive shared task (ADR-0007 one-delete semantic).\n    ///\n    /// Clears `shared_task_id` (tombstone) but RETAINS the local row and its `task_attempt`/run\n    /// artifacts — the hub owns the board, the node never loses local work it ran. This is the\n    /// SINGLE soft-unlink used by BOTH inbound legs — the WS `task.deleted` path (`processor.rs`, via a\n    /// `&mut Transaction`) AND the cold-start/gap-fill reconcile (`node_runner.rs`, via a `&SqlitePool`) —\n    /// so a hive soft-delete yields ONE node outcome regardless of which leg applies it. Executor-generic\n    /// (mirrors `set_shared_task_id`) so the tx-based caller can pass `tx.as_mut()`.\n    /// Returns the number of rows unlinked.\n    pub async fn unlink_by_shared_task_id<'e, E>(\n        executor: E,\n        shared_task_id: Uuid,\n    ) -> Result<u64, sqlx::Error>\n    where\n        E: Executor<'e, Database = Sqlite>,\n    {\n        let result = sqlx::query!(\n            r#\"UPDATE tasks\n               SET shared_task_id = NULL, updated_at = CURRENT_TIMESTAMP\n               WHERE shared_task_id = ?\"#,\n            shared_task_id\n        )\n        .execute(executor)\n        .await?;\n        Ok(result.rows_affected())\n    }\n\n    /// Soft-unlink shared tasks no longer present in the reconcile snapshot (ADR-0007).\n    ///\n    /// The stale-sweep analogue of `unlink_by_shared_task_id`: any task in this project whose\n    /// `shared_task_id` is NOT in the active set is unlinked (cleared) rather than hard-deleted,\n    /// preserving local attempts. Only touches rows that HAVE a `shared_task_id` (hive-synced),\n    /// leaving locally-created tasks untouched. Returns the number of rows unlinked.\n    pub async fn unlink_stale_shared_tasks(\n        pool: &SqlitePool,\n        project_id: Uuid,\n        active_shared_task_ids: &[Uuid],\n    ) -> Result<u64, sqlx::Error> {\n        if active_shared_task_ids.is_empty() {\n            return Ok(0);\n        }\n\n        let placeholders: Vec<String> = active_shared_task_ids\n            .iter()\n            .enumerate()\n            .map(|(i, _)| format!(\"${}\", i + 2))\n            .collect();\n        let placeholders_str = placeholders.join(\", \");\n\n        let query = format!(\n            r#\"UPDATE tasks\n               SET shared_task_id = NULL, updated_at = CURRENT_TIMESTAMP\n               WHERE project_id = $1\n               AND shared_task_id IS NOT NULL\n               AND shared_task_id NOT IN ({})\"#,\n            placeholders_str\n        );\n\n        let mut query_builder = sqlx::query(&query).bind(project_id);\n        for id in active_shared_task_ids {\n            query_builder = query_builder.bind(id);\n        }\n\n        let result = query_builder.execute(pool).await?;\n        Ok(result.rows_affected())\n    }\n\n    /// Clear shared_task_id for orphaned tasks.\n```\n\n### 2. `crates/services/src/services/node_runner.rs` — reconcile leg calls soft-unlink\n- **File:** `crates/services/src/services/node_runner.rs`\n- **Anchor:** (Reuse this module's existing processor/test\n        // harness — see the task.updated / task.deleted tests already present; mirror their setup.)\n        // ...build `processor`, `local_project` (remote_project_id = R), `local_task` (shared_task_id = S)...\n\n        let new_assignee = uuid::Uuid::new_v4();\n        let event = make_task_activity_event(\n            \"task.reassigned\",\n            /* shared task id */ S,\n            /* remote project id */ R,\n            /* version */ 2,\n            /* assignee_user_id */ Some(new_assignee),\n        );\n\n        processor.process_event(event).await.unwrap();\n\n        let after = Task::find_by_shared_task_id(&processor.db.pool, S).await.unwrap().unwrap();\n        assert_eq!(\n            after.remote_assignee_user_id, Some(new_assignee),\n            \"task.reassigned is APPLIED (routed through process_task_upsert_event), not dropped\",\n        );\n        assert_eq!(after.remote_version, 2);\n    }\n```\n> Mirror the EXISTING `task.updated`/`task.deleted` tests in this module for the harness (`processor`\n> construction, `SharedTaskActivityPayload` JSON builder, project/task linking). It is the\n> divergence-detection probe; the heal is 503 (hive reply) + 504 (node acts). \"On reconnect\" is folded\n> into \"the first `sync_once` after (re)connect\" (the 30s loop drives `sync_once` each tick; a reconnect\n> re-establishes the command channel and the next tick emits a fresh digest). Add a NEW method beside the\n  existing `find_*` reads.\n- **Sibling read (rubric #9):** the existing `find_*` methods in THIS file are the pattern — `query!`\n  (NOT `query_as!` into `Task`, since we return a lean projection), `&SqlitePool` arg, BLOB-UUID select\n  casts (`id as \"id!: Uuid\"`), `remote_version as \"remote_version!: i64\"`. Read-only; ordered by `id` for a stable digest. `limit` bounds the batch.\n    pub async fn find_digest_entries(\n        pool: &SqlitePool,\n        limit: i64,\n    ) -> Result<Vec<TaskDigestRow>, sqlx::Error> {\n        sqlx::query!(\n            r#\"SELECT id as \"id!: Uuid\", remote_version as \"remote_version!: i64\"\n               FROM tasks\n               WHERE shared_task_id IS NOT NULL AND archived_at IS NULL\n               ORDER BY id ASC\n               LIMIT ?\"#,\n            limit\n        )\n        .fetch_all(pool)\n        .await\n        .map(|rows| {\n            rows.into_iter()\n                .map(|r| TaskDigestRow { id: r.id, remote_version: r.remote_version })\n                .collect()\n        })\n    }\n}\n```\n> `shared_task_id IS NOT NULL` is the node-side id-bridge predicate (the task has been synced to the\n> hive, so the hive SHOULD have a matching `shared_tasks` row keyed by `source_node_id + source_task_id =\n> this node + id`). A node-linked task the hive lost is exactly the node-has/hive-lacks divergence TS4\n> seeds. Use `id` (local) as `entity_id` — NOT `shared_task_id` — because the bridge key the hive\n> compares against is `source_task_id` = the node's LOCAL id (`shared_tasks` migration\n> `20260105120000`; comment \"Original local task ID from source node\").\n\n### 2. `crates/services/src/services/hive_sync.rs` — build + send the digest each cycle\n- **File:** `crates/services/src/services/hive_sync.rs`\n- **Anchor:** `sync_once` (tail — 107 added a `self.sync_outbox()` call there; place the digest call\n  AFTER it), and the `use super::hive_client::{…}` import block. `DigestEntry` is the WS\n  `crate::services::hive_client::DigestEntry` from 501.\n- **Sibling read (rubric #9):** 107's `sync_outbox` helper in THIS file is the exact template — read from\n  `self.pool`, build a `NodeMessage`, push via `self.command_tx.send(...)`, best-effort, no ack. Read-only — does NOT mark anything synced/acked. Runs every cycle (so \"on reconnect\" =\n        // the first cycle after the channel is re-established); the heal is applied by 504.\n        if let Err(e) = self.sync_digest().await {\n            warn!(error = ?e, \"Failed to send anti-entropy digest\");\n        }\n\n        Ok(())\n    }\n\n    /// Build and push the SC5 anti-entropy digest: one `DigestEntry` per swarm-linked task\n    /// (`shared_task_id IS NOT NULL`) carrying its `remote_version`. Best-effort, read-only; an empty\n    /// set sends nothing. Does NOT advance any cursor (it is divergence DETECTION, not sync).\n    async fn sync_digest(&self) -> Result<(), HiveSyncError> {\n        use db::models::task::Task;\n        let rows = Task::find_digest_entries(&self.pool, self.config.max_tasks_per_batch).await?;\n        if rows.is_empty() {\n            return Ok(());\n        }\n        let entries: Vec<DigestEntry> = rows\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|r| DigestEntry {\n                entity_type: \"task\".to_string(),\n                entity_id: r.id,\n                version: r.remote_version,\n            })\n            .collect();\n        self.command_tx\n            .send(NodeMessage::Digest { entries })\n            .await\n            .map_err(|e| HiveSyncError::Send(e.to_string()))?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n```\n> `HiveSyncError::Send` already exists (107 used it). It is the\n> divergence-detection probe; the heal is 503 (hive reply) + 504 (node acts). \"On reconnect\" is folded\n> into \"the first `sync_once` after (re)connect\" (the 30s loop drives `sync_once` each tick; a reconnect\n> re-establishes the command channel and the next tick emits a fresh digest). Read-only; ordered by `id` for a stable digest. `limit` bounds the batch.\n    pub async fn find_digest_entries(\n        pool: &SqlitePool,\n        limit: i64,\n    ) -> Result<Vec<TaskDigestRow>, sqlx::Error> {\n        sqlx::query!(\n            r#\"SELECT id as \"id!: Uuid\", remote_version as \"remote_version!: i64\"\n               FROM tasks\n               WHERE shared_task_id IS NOT NULL AND archived_at IS NULL\n               ORDER BY id ASC\n               LIMIT ?\"#,\n            limit\n        )\n        .fetch_all(pool)\n        .await\n        .map(|rows| {\n            rows.into_iter()\n                .map(|r| TaskDigestRow { id: r.id, remote_version: r.remote_version })\n                .collect()\n        })\n    }\n}\n```\n> `shared_task_id IS NOT NULL` is the node-side id-bridge predicate (the task has been synced to the\n> hive, so the hive SHOULD have a matching `shared_tasks` row keyed by `source_node_id + source_task_id =\n> this node + id`). A node-linked task the hive lost is exactly the node-has/hive-lacks divergence TS4\n> seeds. Use `id` (local) as `entity_id` — NOT `shared_task_id` — because the bridge key the hive\n> compares against is `source_task_id` = the node's LOCAL id (`shared_tasks` migration\n> `20260105120000`; comment \"Original local task ID from source node\").\n\n### 2. `crates/services/src/services/hive_sync.rs` — build + send the digest each cycle\n- **File:** `crates/services/src/services/hive_sync.rs`\n- **Anchor:** `sync_once` (tail — 107 added a `self.sync_outbox()` call there; place the digest call\n  AFTER it), and the `use super::hive_client::{…}` import block. `DigestEntry` is the WS\n  `crate::services::hive_client::DigestEntry` from 501.\n- **Sibling read (rubric #9):** 107's `sync_outbox` helper in THIS file is the exact template — read from\n  `self.pool`, build a `NodeMessage`, push via `self.command_tx.send(...)`, best-effort, no ack. Best-effort, read-only; an empty\n    /// set sends nothing. Does NOT advance any cursor (it is divergence DETECTION, not sync).\n    async fn sync_digest(&self) -> Result<(), HiveSyncError> {\n        use db::models::task::Task;\n        let rows = Task::find_digest_entries(&self.pool, self.config.max_tasks_per_batch).await?;\n        if rows.is_empty() {\n            return Ok(());\n        }\n        let entries: Vec<DigestEntry> = rows\n            .into_iter()\n            .map(|r| DigestEntry {\n                entity_type: \"task\".to_string(),\n                entity_id: r.id,\n                version: r.remote_version,\n            })\n            .collect();\n        self.command_tx\n            .send(NodeMessage::Digest { entries })\n            .await\n            .map_err(|e| HiveSyncError::Send(e.to_string()))?;\n        Ok(())\n    }\n```\n> `HiveSyncError::Send` already exists (107 used it).
